  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d11cafc5-c331-4f8a-9beb-9c6072c2042a'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText14603622527655341520" style="display:none">A fresh new look for the best-selling series from America’s number-one inspirational novelist, Karen Kingsbury. Fans will enjoy a personal note from Karen and Gary Smalley as well as discussion questions for book group use. As the family looks forward to a heartwarming reunion, they find out that Mr. and Mrs. Baxter have a secret that could change their lives forever.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11663855006809881173">The Redemtpion series is wonderful. <br/>There are so many true to life examples in them that they could touch and change anyone's lives. <br/><br/>I can't capture everything I feel about this series in mere words. If I could put words on what my heart has read and is now digesting, it still wouldn't be sufficient.<br/><br/>Even if you don't think you are a Karen Kingsbury fan, please reconsider this one time and read this series.<br/><br/>I can't wait to go on to the Firstborn series and get more food for my soul.</span>

<div id="review_76252877" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76252877" />
    <a title="LadyCalico" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2288360-ladycalico"><img alt="LadyCalico" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241539428p2/2288360.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76252877?book_show_action=true">Oct 30, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LadyCalico" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LadyCalico" href="/user/show/2288360-ladycalico">LadyCalico</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76252877" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10265738723853940043">My library had only two of the five books of this series--Remember and Reunion. Remember wasn't so hot, but Reunion was better. This series seriously overemphasizes the importance of physical beauty, which struck me as sadly superficial to be so hung up on surface values. I was ambivalence about this book. Much in the story felt soapish, juvenile, and often contrived and unrealistic. Her adult characters are ridiculously immature, and I was repelled by adult Christians responding hysterically an</span>
  <span id="freeText10265738723853940043" style="display:none">My library had only two of the five books of this series--Remember and Reunion. Remember wasn't so hot, but Reunion was better. This series seriously overemphasizes the importance of physical beauty, which struck me as sadly superficial to be so hung up on surface values. I was ambivalence about this book. Much in the story felt soapish, juvenile, and often contrived and unrealistic. Her adult characters are ridiculously immature, and I was repelled by adult Christians responding hysterically and rather meanly to some difficulty, with the maturity of a 13-year old. Personally, I haven't noticed that the Christians in real life respond more histrionically to problems; actually quite the opposite, but Kingsbury characters do way too much emotional over-reacting and not nearly enough pro-active thinking and doing--just deal with it like other adult humans do! However, when the characters finally do get around to seeking answers in prayer, Scripture, and counseling and start to think and communicate, some actual maturity and biblical insights emerge--they just take so long to get there! On the plus side the Bible lessons she works into the solutions to her problems are right-on once she finally gets around to them. If I ever read any other Kingsbury books I will have learned the necessity of skimming over the juvenile hysterical junk and seek out the meat of the scriptural life lesson. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10265738723853940043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_646453627" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646453627" />
    <a title="Mayda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5054798-mayda"><img alt="Mayda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524153792p2/5054798.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646453627?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayda" href="/user/show/5054798-mayda">Mayda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781593558529" href="/book/show/2959028-reunion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5054798-mayda?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5054798-mayda?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5054798-mayda?shelf=christian">christian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646453627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6424823282551377060">This is the fifth book in the series, but I have a feeling that it is not the end of Baxter family saga. Each book in the series focuses on a different sibling and their problems, but none of the books is really a stand-alone tale. The story threads seem to continue into the following books. In this final book, the matriarch of the family is tragically ill, and how she and the family cope with her sickness is the crux of the novel. But there is a secondary story of a secret that the parents have</span>
  <span id="freeText6424823282551377060" style="display:none">This is the fifth book in the series, but I have a feeling that it is not the end of Baxter family saga. Each book in the series focuses on a different sibling and their problems, but none of the books is really a stand-alone tale. The story threads seem to continue into the following books. In this final book, the matriarch of the family is tragically ill, and how she and the family cope with her sickness is the crux of the novel. But there is a secondary story of a secret that the parents have been keeping from their children. This series has an overall feel of a Christian soap opera, if there is such a thing, with all the overwhelming emotions and strong Christian “preachiness,” but not very compelling writing. The plots are predictable for the most part and as well as trite, and I’m not sure, but it seems like the characters never do anything – and I mean ANYTHING – without praying about it and TELLING you they are praying about it. This series is heavy-handed in its witnessing but missed the mark as well-written inspirational Christian fiction.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6424823282551377060" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LaRea Anderson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LaRea Anderson" href="/user/show/50823630-larea-anderson">LaRea Anderson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50823630-larea-anderson?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50823630-larea-anderson?shelf=hoopla">hoopla</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2757072147" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer952662038136235088">I started the Redemption series of the Baxter Family Drama March 4. I love everything about this series. I am a new convert to the Karen Kingsbury fan club, and I can’t believe it took me this long to hop on board. The series plays out like a faith based soap opera, each book centering around a different Baxter, while intertwining the stories of the others within. I read most of these as e-editions, but am working toward purchasing copies for my personal library. This a series I will revisit man</span>
  <span id="freeText952662038136235088" style="display:none">I started the Redemption series of the Baxter Family Drama March 4. I love everything about this series. I am a new convert to the Karen Kingsbury fan club, and I can’t believe it took me this long to hop on board. The series plays out like a faith based soap opera, each book centering around a different Baxter, while intertwining the stories of the others within. I read most of these as e-editions, but am working toward purchasing copies for my personal library. This a series I will revisit many times over the years. I love the writing style, the “realness” of this series. Being a follower of Christ doesn’t save us from heartache. It doesn’t mean life is sunshine, roses, and rainbows. When our faith falters we are always welcome back, redemption waiting. Even though we aren’t saved from heartache, we never have to go through it alone. That is portrayed so beautifully through this series. </span>
  <a data-text-id="952662038136235088" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4783109483059617436" style="display:none">In this book all of the Baxter children return for a dinner. It had been awhile since all of them had been together in one setting. They are finally happy when they find out that their mother has cancer. She will not be able to fight it off. As they wait for a miracle, we see that they had a big secret. They had had a child before marriage, but had given him up for adoption because they were too young. He is a famous actor, but cannot find his biological parents. He has tried many times, but always gets dead ended. Finally, he learns that his mother has cancer and does not have long to live. He goes to see her, and sees her right before she dies. Her last wish was to see him before she died. John, his father, goes in to check on her and she tries to explain that she had seen him. He automatically thinks it is the cancer spreading throughout her body. <br /><br />This book reminds me of how the love of a family can conquer anything. All of the children set aside their own personal feelings when they found out their mother was severely sick. They had a great unity in the end, and it was definitely breath taking.</span>

  <span id="freeText9658249545525077495" style="display:none">I loved getting an insight into the lives of John and Elizabeth Baxter, the mother and father of the Baxter family i have come to "know" and "love" through reading all the Baxter family books. This whole series managed to show what true faith really is and I can see these books touching many hearts for God and showing the difference between Love and religion :)</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2172966367?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne Marie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne Marie" href="/user/show/11986319-anne-marie">Anne Marie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2172966367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15713056018081638565">This book was wonderful like the rest of the series but very difficult to read. It was primarily about Elizabeth Baxter, mother and matriarch of the Baxter family, losing her battle with cancer. Since I’ve read the Sunrise series, I knew she was going to pass away, but struggled along with the family and never lost hope for a miracle. I also noticed on the front cover of the book the grave stone in the Baxter’s backyard. If this is supposed to be Elizabeth’s, next to the bench her and John would</span>
  <span id="freeText15713056018081638565" style="display:none">This book was wonderful like the rest of the series but very difficult to read. It was primarily about Elizabeth Baxter, mother and matriarch of the Baxter family, losing her battle with cancer. Since I’ve read the Sunrise series, I knew she was going to pass away, but struggled along with the family and never lost hope for a miracle. I also noticed on the front cover of the book the grave stone in the Baxter’s backyard. If this is supposed to be Elizabeth’s, next to the bench her and John would spend talking on, it doesn’t make sense because in the Sunrise series the family would visit a cemetery with a bench beside the grave. Anyway, the family gets to say their goodbyes, but a secret between Elizabeth and John remains. They gave up their first born son when Elizabeth got pregnant before they were married. They tried to locate him when Elizabeth first battled cancer in the 90’s, but had no luck. Instead, Dayne Matthews, movie star, finds Elizabeth. Through a series of coincidences, Dayne’s entertainment lawyer is in a firm where Luke Baxter is working as an intern/part-time, before he gets his law degree. Dayne is introduced to Luke and they have no problem having a conversation. When Luke shows Dayne pictures of his family and his mother, Dayne is struck with a knowing that he’s seen Elizabeth’s picture before. He finds a box marked adoption papers in a storage unit he kept with his parents’ belongings. (His parents were killed in a plane crash doing missionary work.) In the box is a picture that resembles the picture that was on Luke’s desk. Only after hiring a private investigator is the truth confirmed...Elizabeth is his birth mother, the Baxter’s his family. Dayne is able to arrive at his mother’s bedside hours before her death, and they are able to meet for the first time, alone. A nurse sees him, but thinks he is Luke. <br />Ashley and Landon get married. They have to move up their wedding a week earlier due to Elizabeth’s impending death, but the day turns out perfectly. <br />Kari and Ryan have the Flanigan family over for dinner. We are introduced to the family. Jim works with Ryan coaching football at the college. <br />Brooke and Peter’s daughter, Hayley, continues to make progress from her drowning. <br />Erin and Sam are living in Texas. They are waiting to adopt a baby girl, but the baby’s mother, boyfriend, and his friend make Adam and Erin pay them an extra $5000 for “expenses.” Only when they ask for another large amount of money do they call the authorities. Then when the baby is born, the biological mother, Candy, refuses to give up her daughter. But as time passes, Candy gets more addicted to drugs, and leaves her baby with a neighbor to take care of. She doesn’t return, and in the meantime, she gets arrested for shooting a man in a drug deal. Because of her jail sentence, and because Candy’s mother will be working on a cruise ship, Erin and Sam not only can adopt the baby, Amy Elizabeth, but also her two sisters, Chloe and Clarisse. Erin and Sam also adopt a baby that was abandoned by its mother who they name Heidi Joe! So they now have four daughters! </span>
  <a data-text-id="15713056018081638565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4370815958748478010">I skipped three novels in the Redemption series since most of them were on waiting list in the library but this book gave a fair summary of what have transpired in the other novels. I liked the story and the struggle, which is <b>very deep and haunting</b>. I think <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3159984.Karen_Kingsbury' title='Karen Kingsbury' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karen Kingsbury</a> did well in doing a summary of the series but also hinted on the plot for the next coming series. <br/><br/>Since most of the character development were done in the earlier novels, I did feel there was a lack of serious engagement with</span>
  <span id="freeText4370815958748478010" style="display:none">I skipped three novels in the Redemption series since most of them were on waiting list in the library but this book gave a fair summary of what have transpired in the other novels. I liked the story and the struggle, which is <b>very deep and haunting</b>. I think <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3159984.Karen_Kingsbury" title="Karen Kingsbury" rel="nofollow noopener">Karen Kingsbury</a> did well in doing a summary of the series but also hinted on the plot for the next coming series. <br /><br />Since most of the character development were done in the earlier novels, I did feel there was a lack of serious engagement with the readers who hasn't touched on the other novels. The multiple plots running parallel can also be daunting to follow and is <i>emotionally taxing</i> but taking a couple a chapter at a time, it helped me finish the book. It also helped me understand that <i>many people go through such events in the real world</i> without break, family and any support. <br /><br />I'm grateful for this summary and willing to look into the other series, as soon as I finish the other novels in Redemption series. I do recommend reading this book even if many are saying that it is a depressing book. If it seemed sad for an <i>"ending"</i> then look forward to the next series. This is a good book to <u>read during Easter</u> because that's how it felt to me at the end of the book. <b>
  <i>You never end Easter at Jesus' crucifixion but in his resurrection and his promise to come back for those who love him.</i>
</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="4370815958748478010" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3543083485968830121">The final book in Karen Kingsbury’s “Redemption” was a brilliant conclusion to the series. Elizabeth Baxter has lived many years without her cancer arising again but as they say, all good things must come to an end. The Baxter family plans for a reunion knowing deep down that this may be the last reunion where everyone will be there. As the reunion plans are underway, so are the plans for a wonderful wedding. As Elizabeth battles the cancer, memories of her biggest secret come to mind constantly</span>
  <span id="freeText3543083485968830121" style="display:none">The final book in Karen Kingsbury’s “Redemption” was a brilliant conclusion to the series. Elizabeth Baxter has lived many years without her cancer arising again but as they say, all good things must come to an end. The Baxter family plans for a reunion knowing deep down that this may be the last reunion where everyone will be there. As the reunion plans are underway, so are the plans for a wonderful wedding. As Elizabeth battles the cancer, memories of her biggest secret come to mind constantly. Off in Hollywood, a famous actor named Dayne Matthews, hunts down the remaining fragments of his past. The results shock him but at the same time excites him. Experiencing the sorrow and pain of the Baxter family was surprisingly a highlight of the book. Throughout the series, the reader grows connected to the characters and the ending was just as emotional as all the other books. I recommend this book for anyone who wants to finish the series or wants to see real family love, pure and whole.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2141129821" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2141129821" />
    <a title="Betty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61666158-betty"><img alt="Betty" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2141129821?book_show_action=true">Oct 06, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betty" href="/user/show/61666158-betty">Betty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio CD 9781593558536" href="/book/show/14474766-reunion">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2141129821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7216078623641823352">I am never disappointed with Karen Kingsbury and the beautiful way she brings the stories together. It was sad to have Elizabeth die but the experiences in her books mirror the experiences we encounter in our walk in our own lives. She truly has a gift for writing, allowing the Christian thoughts and scriptures to work their way throughout. Yes, I cry, and it take me longer to read through the tears but they are good tears. I loved the story!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2412680921" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13102869037057537645">This was my favorite of the redemption series. It reminded me to be thankful every day for my husband, daughter, and-granddaughters. I really like how close the family is and how much they care and support one another. Ashley was my favorite character. The new series is the Firstborn series which is about more characters in the Baxter family. I’m looking forward to read that series. For me it is just uplifting to read Karen’s books. </span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13052882319090400570">This was my second read of this series. The first time through I truly struggled with Reunion due to the subject matter. This time I was prepared for the tears and still struggled a bit, but was able to see through the sad parts to the message of the book. I've also finally learned my lesson: never read a Karen Kingsbury book without a box of tissues handy!</span>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('DPKucd9OP2yLJkj9R3OlkDBHx7jm0/iy3kAviUZj8xTNxZ2bAhG4UC0KDgX5qoYaXVPCxIbySPQorPVHDP4dsg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QtJM8rrdiIrhuuPNeMm9IwcHON1w/jl8DbDeIRJ1G8SD5X8YZ4IPtkeWpTXGEJ6pahM9oRDfiTr7XATvWOj1Yg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer13584777487952965192">Karen Kingsbury, #1 New York Times bestselling novelist, is America’s favorite inspirational storyteller, with more than twenty-five million copies of her award-winning books in print. Her last dozen titles have topped bestseller lists and many of her novels are under development with Hallmark Films and as major motion pictures. Her Baxter Family books are being developed into a TV series slated f</span>
  <span id="freeText13584777487952965192" style="display:none">Karen Kingsbury, #1 New York Times bestselling novelist, is America’s favorite inspirational storyteller, with more than twenty-five million copies of her award-winning books in print. Her last dozen titles have topped bestseller lists and many of her novels are under development with Hallmark Films and as major motion pictures. Her Baxter Family books are being developed into a TV series slated for major network viewing sometime in the next year. Karen is also an adjunct professor of writing at Liberty University. In 2001 she and her husband, Don, adopted three boys from Haiti, doubling their family in a matter of months. Today the couple has joined the ranks of empty nesters, living in Tennessee near five of their adult children.<br /><br />See more at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://authors.simonandschuster.com/Karen-Kingsbury/82982459#sthash.sM45tLbq.dpuf">http://authors.simonandschuster.com/K...</a></span>

      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('bookCover_11430').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_11430').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_11430').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {

            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
